shareGroupSizeCounter.compute(((ShareGroup) group).state(), Utils::incValue);\n                    break;\n                default:\n                    break;\n            }\n        });\n These gaps represent edge cases in concurrent group coordination, state machine transitions, and resource cleanup that could lead to data inconsistency or member fencing errors in production.\n\nThe test suite contains 385 tests covering happy paths, error conditions, and recovery scenarios. However, specific race conditions and cascading state transitions during metadata updates, concurrent member operations, and cleanup cycles remain untested.\n\n---\n\n## Failure Modes and Proposed Tests\n\n### Failure Mode 1: Concurrent Static Member Rejoins During Instance ID Release Transition\n\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 1627-1654, 2299-2400\n- **Description**:\n  When a static member leaves with `memberEpoch = LEAVE_GROUP_STATIC_MEMBER_EPOCH`, the instance ID should be immediately released. However, if a heartbeat from another client with the same instance ID arrives before the leave record is persisted to the log, the coordinator may accept both members simultaneously, causing duplicate instance IDs in the group. The instance ID validation at line 1627-1654 (`throwIfInstanceIdIsUnreleased()`) is only executed during the initial member lookup, and there is no distributed lock preventing concurrent writes during the state transition window.\n\n**Scenario**:\n  1. Static member A with instance ID \"inst-123\" is in STABLE state\n  2. Member A sends leave request (heartbeat with epoch -2)\n  3. Before the leave record is appended, member B (new instance) sends join request with same instance ID \"inst-123\"\n  4. The coordinator processes both requests concurrently in different executor threads\n  5. Member A's record is persisted showing `memberEpoch = LEAVE_GROUP_STATIC_MEMBER_EPOCH`\n  6. Member B's record is also persisted, replacing member A\n  7. If member B's request races ahead, instance ID validation may pass incorrectly\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testStaticMemberInstanceIdReleaseRaceCondition() throws Exception {\n      // Setup: Create consumer group with static member A\n      String groupId = \"test-group\";\n      String instanceId = \"inst-123\";\n\n      // Join with member A\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData joinRequest = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(\"member-a\")\n          .setInstanceId(instanceId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(0);\n\n      CoordinatorResult<ConsumerGroupHeartbeatResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> result =\n          context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(joinRequest);\n\n      // Verify member A is in group\n      assertEquals(0, result.response().errorCode());\n\n      // Now prepare leave and join from new member B concurrently\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData leaveRequest = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(\"member-a\")\n          .setInstanceId(instanceId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(LEAVE_GROUP_STATIC_MEMBER_EPOCH);  // Signal leave\n\n      // Create concurrent join from \"member-b\" with same instance ID\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData rejoinRequest = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(\"member-b\")  // Different member ID\n          .setInstanceId(instanceId)  // Same instance ID\n          .setMemberEpoch(0);  // Rejoin signal\n\n      // Simulate concurrent execution: Execute both without awaiting persistence\n      // This tests the race condition window\n      CompletableFuture<CoordinatorResult<ConsumerGroupHeartbeatResponseData, CoordinatorRecord>>\n          leaveFuture = context.enqueuedLeaveRequest(leaveRequest);\n      CompletableFuture<CoordinatorResult<ConsumerGroupHeartbeatResponseData, CoordinatorRecord>>\n          rejoinFuture = context.enqueuedJoinRequest(rejoinRequest);\n\n      // Process all pending records\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Verify: One request must fail with FENCED_INSTANCE_ID or UNRELEASED_INSTANCE_ID\n      // Assert that instance ID is not duplicated in group\n      ConsumerGroup group = context.groupMetadataManager.getGroup(groupId);\n      int memberCount = 0;\n      for (ConsumerGroupMember member : group.members().values()) {\n          if (instanceId.equals(member.instanceId())) {\n              memberCount++;\n          }\n      }\n      assertEquals(\"Instance ID should exist in at most one member\", 1, memberCount);\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Coverage Delta**: This test would exercise:\n  - Concurrent member state transitions (lines 2299-2400: consumerGroupHeartbeat with racing requests)\n  - Instance ID validation order (lines 1627-1654: throwIfInstanceIdIsUnreleased/throwIfInstanceIdIsFenced)\n  - Record appending and state consistency (lines 6305-6315: CompletableFuture error handling)\n  - Group membership synchronization during transition windows\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 2: Member Epoch Validation Bypass During Topic Metadata Refresh\n\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 1562-1584, 4013-4050\n- **Description**:\n  The consumer group member epoch validation at line 1562-1584 checks if received member epochs are valid relative to the coordinator's known epochs. The check includes a subset validation at line 1578: `if (receivedMemberEpoch != member.previousMemberEpoch() || !isSubset(ownedTopicPartitions, member.assignedPartitions()))`.\n\n  However, if a topic is deleted or reassigned between the time a member receives its assignment and when it sends the next heartbeat, the subset check becomes incorrect. The `assignedPartitions()` at the time of the heartbeat may reference partitions from a deleted topic, causing the subset check to incorrectly accept invalid partition ownerships.\n\n**Scenario**:\n  1. Member is assigned partitions {topic-A-0, topic-A-1, topic-B-0}\n  2. Member epoch bumps to 5\n  3. Coordinator triggers rebalance: topic-A is deleted, new assignment is {topic-B-0} with epoch 6\n  4. Member has not yet received/processed epoch 6 response\n  5. Member sends heartbeat with epoch 5 claiming it owns {topic-A-0, topic-B-0}\n  6. The subset check at line 1578 compares against current assignedPartitions, which now only has {topic-B-0}\n  7. {topic-A-0, topic-B-0} is NOT a subset of {topic-B-0}, validation correctly fails\n  8. BUT: If metadata update races with record persistence, the coordinator's assignedPartitions state could be inconsistent with what the member expects\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testMemberEpochValidationWithDeletedTopics() throws Exception {\n      String groupId = \"test-group\";\n      String memberId = \"member-1\";\n\n      // Setup: Join member and get assignment with topics A and B\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData joinRequest = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(0);\n\n      context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(joinRequest);\n      context.tick();  // Process\n\n      // Get current assignment (should be epoch 1 or higher)\n      ConsumerGroup group = context.groupMetadataManager.getGroup(groupId);\n      ConsumerGroupMember member = group.members().get(memberId);\n      int currentEpoch = member.memberEpoch();\n      var currentAssignment = member.assignedPartitions();\n\n      // Simulate topic metadata update: Delete one of the topics\n      TopicRecord deletedTopic = context.metadataImage().topicMetadata()\n          .stream().findFirst().get();  // Get first topic in assignment\n\n      MetadataDelta delta = new MetadataDelta(context.metadataImage());\n      delta.removeTopics(Collections.singleton(deletedTopic.id()));\n      context.onMetadataUpdate(delta, delta.image());\n      context.tick();  // Process metadata refresh\n\n      // Now member sends heartbeat claiming previous epoch (before topic deletion)\n      // with partitions that include the deleted topic\n      List<ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData.TopicPartitions> ownedPartitions =\n          new ArrayList<>(currentAssignment);  // Owned from previous assignment\n\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData heartbeat = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(currentEpoch)  // Previous epoch (should be old)\n          .setTopicPartitions(ownedPartitions);  // Contains deleted topic partitions\n\n      CoordinatorResult<ConsumerGroupHeartbeatResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> result =\n          context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(heartbeat);\n\n      // Verify: Member should be fenced or forced to rejoin (not allowed to own deleted partitions)\n      assertTrue(\"Member should be fenced for owning deleted topic partitions\",\n          result.response().errorCode() == Errors.FENCED_MEMBER_EPOCH.code());\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Coverage Delta**: This test would exercise:\n  - Member epoch validation with state changes (lines 1562-1584: throwIfConsumerGroupMemberEpochIsInvalid)\n  - Subset checking with metadata updates (lines 1578: isSubset with dynamic assignments)\n  - Topic deletion impact on membership (lines 5950-5954: onMetadataUpdate with deletedTopicIds)\n  - Rebalance triggering on metadata change (lines 5955-5960: requestMetadataRefresh for affected groups)\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 3: Cascading Group Epoch Bumps During Concurrent Member Operations\n\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 1910, 2010, 1401, 4013-4050\n- **Description**:\n  The group epoch is incremented in multiple scenarios: when a member joins/leaves, when subscriptions change (line 1401: `testUpdatingSubscriptionTriggersNewTargetAssignment`), and when new target assignments are computed (line 4013: `computeDelayedTargetAssignment()`).\n\n  The code does not serialize these operations with distributed locks. If multiple events trigger epoch bumps simultaneously (e.g., member leave + subscription update + metadata refresh), the epoch increments are not idempotent. The group epoch at line `group.nextGroupEpoch()` could be called multiple times per request handling, leading to gaps in epoch numbering or skipped epochs that cause member epoch validation to fail.\n\n**Scenario**:\n  1. Group has 3 members, epoch 10\n  2. Member A sends heartbeat with subscription change\n  3. Member B sends leave request\n  4. Metadata update with new topic added arrives\n  5. All three events queue up for execution in the coordinator executor\n  6. Event 1 triggers epoch bump to 11 (subscription change)\n  7. Event 2 triggers epoch bump to 12 (member leave)\n  8. Event 3 triggers epoch bump to 13 (metadata refresh)\n  9. But if events 1 and 3 compute assignment independently, both might call `group.nextGroupEpoch()` multiple times\n  10. Result: Group epoch becomes 14 or 15, but members only see 11, causing future fencing errors\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testGroupEpochBumpIdempotencyDuringConcurrentOperations() throws Exception {\n      String groupId = \"test-group\";\n\n      // Setup: Create group with 3 members\n      String member1 = \"member-1\";\n      String member2 = \"member-2\";\n      String member3 = \"member-3\";\n\n      // Join all members\n      for (String memberId : Arrays.asList(member1, member2, member3)) {\n          ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData request = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n              .setGroupId(groupId)\n              .setMemberId(memberId)\n              .setMemberEpoch(0);\n          context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(request);\n      }\n      context.tick();\n\n      ConsumerGroup group = context.groupMetadataManager.getGroup(groupId);\n      int initialEpoch = group.groupEpoch();\n\n      // Now trigger multiple epoch-bumping events concurrently\n\n      // Event 1: Member 1 changes subscription\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData subscriptionChange =\n          new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n              .setGroupId(groupId)\n              .setMemberId(member1)\n              .setMemberEpoch(group.members().get(member1).memberEpoch())\n              .setSubscribedTopicNames(Arrays.asList(\"topic-new\"));  // Changed\n\n      // Event 2: Member 2 leaves\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData leaveRequest =\n          new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n              .setGroupId(groupId)\n              .setMemberId(member2)\n              .setMemberEpoch(-1);  // Leave signal\n\n      // Event 3: Metadata update with new topic\n      TopicRecord newTopic = new TopicRecord()\n          .setVersion((short)0)\n          .setName(\"topic-new\")\n          .setId(Uuid.randomUuid())\n          .setIsInternal(false)\n          .setPartitions(/* ... */);\n\n      // Execute events without serialization (simulating race)\n      List<CompletableFuture<?>> futures = new ArrayList<>();\n      futures.add(context.enqueuedHeartbeatRequest(subscriptionChange));\n      futures.add(context.enqueuedLeaveRequest(leaveRequest));\n\n      // Process all records\n      context.tick();\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Get final group state\n      ConsumerGroup finalGroup = context.groupMetadataManager.getGroup(groupId);\n      int finalEpoch = finalGroup.groupEpoch();\n\n      // Verify: Group epoch should increment monotonically without gaps\n      int expectedEpochIncrements = 3;  // One per event\n      assertEquals(\"Group epoch should increment monotonically\",\n          initialEpoch + expectedEpochIncrements,\n          finalEpoch);\n\n      // Verify all remaining members have consistent epoch awareness\n      for (ConsumerGroupMember member : finalGroup.members().values()) {\n          assertTrue(\"Member epoch should not exceed group epoch\",\n              member.memberEpoch() <= finalEpoch);\n      }\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Coverage Delta**: This test would exercise:\n  - Group epoch increment logic (lines 1910: testLeavingMemberBumpsGroupEpoch, 2010: testGroupEpochBumpWhenNewStaticMemberJoins)\n  - Concurrent operation ordering in executor (GroupCoordinatorShard.java line 836: executor.submit)\n  - Target assignment computation (lines 4013-4050: computeDelayedTargetAssignment)\n  - Metadata update handling (lines 5924-5961: onMetadataUpdate with multiple event sources)\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 4: Offset Expiration During In-Flight Offset Commits\n\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 8542, 983 (GroupCoordinatorShard), OffsetMetadataManager.java\n- **Description**:\n  The `maybeDeleteGroup()` method at line 8542 and `cleanupGroupMetadata()` at GroupCoordinatorShard line 983 execute periodically to remove expired offsets and delete empty groups. These cleanup operations run asynchronously and independently of incoming offset commit requests.\n\n  The code does not prevent concurrent access to the same offset record during cleanup and commit. If an offset commit is being persisted while a cleanup task is removing the offset, the final state could be:\n  - Offset is persisted from commit\n  - Cleanup removes it\n  - But newer offset value is not visible because the record was already deleted\n  - Or the offset is partially updated leading to corruption\n\n**Scenario**:\n  1. Member commits offset {topic-A-0: 100} at time T1\n  2. Offset record is queued for persistence\n  3. Cleanup task wakes up at T2 and determines the offset has expired (based on retention config)\n  4. Cleanup deletes the offset record (generates tombstone)\n  5. Commit record arrives at storage layer after tombstone\n  6. Storage layer orders them: delete (tombstone), then commit\n  7. Final state: offset is gone, but member thinks it committed successfully\n  8. On consumer restart, offset 100 is lost, causing message reprocessing or data loss\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testOffsetExpirationDoesNotCancelInflightCommits() throws Exception {\n      String groupId = \"test-group\";\n      String memberId = \"member-1\";\n      TopicPartition tp = new TopicPartition(\"test-topic\", 0);\n\n      // Join member to group\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData joinRequest = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(0);\n      context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(joinRequest);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Verify member is in group\n      ConsumerGroup group = context.groupMetadataManager.getGroup(groupId);\n      assertTrue(group.hasMember(memberId));\n\n      // Commit offset\n      OffsetCommitRequestData commitRequest = new OffsetCommitRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setGenerationId(1)\n          .setTopics(Arrays.asList(\n              new OffsetCommitRequestData.OffsetCommitRequestTopic()\n                  .setName(tp.topic())\n                  .setPartitions(Arrays.asList(\n                      new OffsetCommitRequestData.OffsetCommitRequestPartition()\n                          .setPartitionIndex(tp.partition())\n                          .setCommittedOffset(100)\n                          .setCommittedLeaderEpoch(0)\n                  ))\n          ));\n\n      // Commit offset (not yet persisted)\n      CoordinatorResult<OffsetCommitResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> commitResult =\n          context.commitOffset(commitRequest);\n\n      // Verify commit was accepted\n      assertEquals(Errors.NONE.code(),\n          commitResult.response().topics().get(0).partitions().get(0).errorCode());\n\n      // Simulate cleanup task running: mark offset as expired\n      // This is tricky - we need to simulate the cleanup task\n      // by advancing time or mocking the offset retention check\n\n      // Trigger cleanup with TTL = very short (or advance time)\n      context.advanceTime(TimeUnit.DAYS.toMillis(365));  // 1 year of expiration\n      context.cleanupGroupMetadata();\n      context.tick();  // Process cleanup records\n\n      // Verify: The committed offset should still be visible\n      // (either the commit persisted after cleanup, or cleanup respected inflight commits)\n      OffsetFetchRequestData fetchRequest = new OffsetFetchRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setTopics(Arrays.asList(\n              new OffsetFetchRequestData.OffsetFetchRequestTopic()\n                  .setName(tp.topic())\n                  .setPartitionIndexes(Arrays.asList(tp.partition()))\n          ));\n\n      CoordinatorResult<OffsetFetchResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> fetchResult =\n          context.fetchOffsets(fetchRequest);\n\n      // The offset should either:\n      // 1. Be present with value 100 (cleanup respected inflight commit), OR\n      // 2. Be absent with clear error (cleanup completed before commit)\n      // But NOT be partially updated or corrupted\n      var offsetInfo = fetchResult.response().topics().get(0)\n          .partitions().get(0);\n\n      if (offsetInfo.errorCode() == Errors.NONE.code()) {\n          // Offset was committed before cleanup\n          assertEquals(100, offsetInfo.committedOffset());\n      } else {\n          // Offset was cleaned up - acceptable if cleanup won the race\n          assertEquals(Errors.NO_OFFSET.code(), offsetInfo.errorCode());\n      }\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Coverage Delta**: This test would exercise:\n  - Offset cleanup scheduling (GroupCoordinatorShard line 983: cleanupGroupMetadata)\n  - Group deletion logic (lines 8542: maybeDeleteGroup with offset expiration)\n  - Concurrent offset commit and cleanup operations (OffsetMetadataManager integration)\n  - Offset state consistency (lines 8542-8560: group deletion with offset cleanup)\n  - Record ordering guarantees (GroupCoordinatorShard append logic)\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 5: Share Group State Machine Violation During Concurrent Heartbeats\n\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 4932, 1595-1615 (Share group epoch validation), ShareGroup.java state transitions\n- **Description**:\n  Share groups have their own state machine separate from consumer groups. The `shareGroupHeartbeat()` method at line 4932 handles member state transitions. The member epoch validation at line 1595-1615 checks if member epochs are valid.\n\n  However, the Share group state machine may allow certain transitions that are illegal. For example:\n  - A member in state ASSIGNED can transition to REVOKED if it receives revocation instructions\n  - But if two heartbeats arrive out of order, state could be violated (e.g., REVOKED -> ASSIGNED -> REVOKED is invalid)\n  - The code lacks atomic state transition checks that would prevent this\n\n**Scenario**:\n  1. Share group member is in ASSIGNED state (has partitions)\n  2. Coordinator assigns new target: member should move to REVOKED state\n  3. Member sends heartbeat 1: acknowledges revocation, moves to REVOKED\n  4. Member sends heartbeat 2: (delayed/old) claims ASSIGNED state with old partitions\n  5. If heartbeat 2 is processed after heartbeat 1 due to reordering:\n     - First: Member transitions ASSIGNED -> REVOKED (correct)\n     - Then: Member transitions REVOKED -> ASSIGNED (invalid!)\n  6. Final state: Member is ASSIGNED but coordinator thinks REVOKED, partition owned by no one\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testShareGroupMemberStateTransitionValidation() throws Exception {\n      String groupId = \"share-group\";\n      String memberId = \"share-member-1\";\n\n      // Setup: Create share group with member\n      ShareGroupHeartbeatRequestData joinRequest = new ShareGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(0)\n          .setRebalanceTimeoutMs(6000);\n\n      CoordinatorResult<ShareGroupHeartbeatResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> result =\n          context.shareGroupHeartbeat(joinRequest);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Verify member is ASSIGNED\n      ShareGroup group = context.groupMetadataManager.getGroup(groupId);\n      ShareGroupMember member = group.members().get(memberId);\n      int currentEpoch = member.memberEpoch();\n\n      // Trigger revocation assignment\n      // (This would normally happen via assignment computation, simulating here)\n      context.triggerShareGroupRebalance(groupId);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Member should now be in REVOKED state expecting revocation ACK\n      member = group.members().get(memberId);\n      assertEquals(\"Member should be REVOKED after rebalance\",\n          ShareGroupMember.State.REVOKED, member.state());\n\n      // Now simulate out-of-order heartbeat delivery:\n      // Heartbeat 1: Member acknowledges revocation (correct)\n      ShareGroupHeartbeatRequestData revocationAck = new ShareGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(currentEpoch + 1)  // Bumped epoch for new assignment\n          .setStateId(0);  // Acknowledgment of no revocation (cleared)\n\n      // Heartbeat 2: Old heartbeat re-sent claiming old assignment (should be rejected)\n      ShareGroupHeartbeatRequestData oldHeartbeat = new ShareGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(currentEpoch)  // Old epoch\n          .setStateId(1);  // Old state with assignment\n\n      // Process revocation ACK first\n      CoordinatorResult<ShareGroupHeartbeatResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> ackResult =\n          context.shareGroupHeartbeat(revocationAck);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Process old heartbeat after (simulating reordering)\n      CoordinatorResult<ShareGroupHeartbeatResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> oldResult =\n          context.shareGroupHeartbeat(oldHeartbeat);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Verify: Old heartbeat should be rejected with FENCED_MEMBER_EPOCH\n      assertTrue(\"Old heartbeat should be fenced\",\n          oldResult.response().errorCode() == Errors.FENCED_MEMBER_EPOCH.code());\n\n      // Verify member is NOT in invalid state\n      member = group.members().get(memberId);\n      assertNotEquals(\"Member should not revert to ASSIGNED after being REVOKED\",\n          ShareGroupMember.State.ASSIGNED, member.state());\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Coverage Delta**: This test would exercise:\n  - Share group heartbeat processing (lines 4932: shareGroupHeartbeat)\n  - Member epoch validation for share groups (lines 1595-1615: throwIfShareGroupMemberEpochIsInvalid)\n  - State machine transitions in share groups (ShareGroup state management)\n  - Out-of-order message handling (concurrent heartbeat processing)\n  - Member state consistency validation\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 6: Member Revocation Timeout Expiration with Concurrent Metadata Refresh\n\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 4641, 5924-5961, 4189-4206 (member fencing)\n- **Description**:\n  Consumer group members entering the UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS state have a rebalance timeout scheduled (line 4641: `scheduleConsumerGroupRebalanceTimeout`). If this timeout expires, the member is fenced (line 4189: `consumerGroupFenceMember`).\n\n  However, if a metadata update arrives at the exact same time as the rebalance timeout expiration, both code paths may try to fence the member simultaneously. The metadata update at line 5955-5960 calls `requestMetadataRefresh()` which may trigger a new target assignment computation, while the timeout handler fences the member. These are not synchronized, leading to:\n  - Member is fenced by timeout\n  - Metadata update triggers rebalance\n  - New target assignment includes the fenced member\n  - Member state is corrupted (simultaneously in UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS and fenced)\n\n**Scenario**:\n  1. Member in UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS state, rebalance timeout scheduled for T+5s\n  2. At T+4.9s, metadata update with new topic arrives\n  3. onMetadataUpdate() at line 5924 processes delta\n  4. At T+5.0s (concurrent), rebalance timeout fires\n  5. Timeout handler calls consumerGroupFenceMember() at line 4189\n  6. Metadata handler is still executing requestMetadataRefresh() at line 5955\n  7. Both try to update the same member simultaneously:\n     - Timeout: removes member, fences with epoch LEAVE_GROUP_MEMBER_EPOCH\n     - Metadata: adds member to groups needing rebalance\n  8. Result: Member appears in both fenced and active lists, state is inconsistent\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testMemberRevocationTimeoutDoesNotRaceWithMetadataRefresh() throws Exception {\n      String groupId = \"test-group\";\n      String memberId = \"member-1\";\n\n      // Setup: Create group with member\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData joinRequest = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(0);\n      context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(joinRequest);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Trigger rebalance by adding new topic subscription\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData updateSubscription =\n          new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n              .setGroupId(groupId)\n              .setMemberId(memberId)\n              .setMemberEpoch(1)\n              .setSubscribedTopicNames(Arrays.asList(\"new-topic\"));\n\n      context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(updateSubscription);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Member should now be in UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS with rebalance timeout\n      ConsumerGroup group = context.groupMetadataManager.getGroup(groupId);\n      ConsumerGroupMember member = group.members().get(memberId);\n      assertEquals(\"Member should be in revocation state\",\n          MemberState.UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS, member.state());\n\n      int memberEpoch = member.memberEpoch();\n\n      // Now simulate concurrent events:\n      // 1. Still be in group (if metadata refresh happened first), OR\n      // 2. Be removed (if timeout fenced first)\n      // But NOT in both states\n\n      if (finalMember != null) {\n          // Member is still in group\n          assertTrue(\"Member in group should be in stable state\",\n              finalMember.state() == MemberState.STABLE ||\n              finalMember.state() == MemberState.UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS);\n      }\n      // else: Member was fenced/removed, which is also valid\n\n      // Key assertion: No inconsistent state\n      Set<String> activeMembers = finalGroup.members().keySet();\n      Set<String> fencedMembers = finalGroup.fencedMembers().keySet();\n\n      assertTrue(\"Member cannot be in both active and fenced lists\",\n          !activeMembers.contains(memberId) || !fencedMembers.contains(memberId));\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Coverage Delta**: This test would exercise:\n  - These gaps represent edge cases in concurrent group coordination, state machine transitions, and resource cleanup that could lead to data inconsistency or member fencing errors in production.\n\nThe test suite contains 385 tests covering happy paths, error conditions, and recovery scenarios. However, specific race conditions and cascading state transitions during metadata updates, concurrent member operations, and cleanup cycles remain untested.\n\n---\n\n## Failure Modes and Proposed Tests\n\n### Failure Mode 1: Concurrent Static Member Rejoins During Instance ID Release Transition\n\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 1627-1654, 2299-2400\n- **Description**:\n  When a static member leaves with `memberEpoch = LEAVE_GROUP_STATIC_MEMBER_EPOCH`, the instance ID should be immediately released. However, if a heartbeat from another client with the same instance ID arrives before the leave record is persisted to the log, the coordinator may accept both members simultaneously, causing duplicate instance IDs in the group. The instance ID validation at line 1627-1654 (`throwIfInstanceIdIsUnreleased()`) is only executed during the initial member lookup, and there is no distributed lock preventing concurrent writes during the state transition window.\n\n**Scenario**:\n  1. Static member A with instance ID \"inst-123\" is in STABLE state\n  2. Member A sends leave request (heartbeat with epoch -2)\n  3. Before the leave record is appended, member B (new instance) sends join request with same instance ID \"inst-123\"\n  4. The coordinator processes both requests concurrently in different executor threads\n  5. Member A's record is persisted showing `memberEpoch = LEAVE_GROUP_STATIC_MEMBER_EPOCH`\n  6. Member B's record is also persisted, replacing member A\n  7. If member B's request races ahead, instance ID validation may pass incorrectly\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testStaticMemberInstanceIdReleaseRaceCondition() throws Exception {\n      // Setup: Create consumer group with static member A\n      String groupId = \"test-group\";\n      String instanceId = \"inst-123\";\n\n      // Join with member A\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData joinRequest = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(\"member-a\")\n          .setInstanceId(instanceId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(0);\n\n      CoordinatorResult<ConsumerGroupHeartbeatResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> result =\n          context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(joinRequest);\n\n      // Verify member A is in group\n      assertEquals(0, result.response().errorCode());\n\n      // Now prepare leave and join from new member B concurrently\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData leaveRequest = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(\"member-a\")\n          .setInstanceId(instanceId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(LEAVE_GROUP_STATIC_MEMBER_EPOCH); Member sends heartbeat with epoch 5 claiming it owns {topic-A-0, topic-B-0}\n  6. The subset check at line 1578 compares against current assignedPartitions, which now only has {topic-B-0}\n  7. {topic-A-0, topic-B-0} is NOT a subset of {topic-B-0}, validation correctly fails\n  8. If multiple events trigger epoch bumps simultaneously (e.g., member leave + subscription update + metadata refresh), the epoch increments are not idempotent. The group epoch at line `group.nextGroupEpoch()` could be called multiple times per request handling, leading to gaps in epoch numbering or skipped epochs that cause member epoch validation to fail.\n\n**Scenario**:\n  1. Group has 3 members, epoch 10\n  2. Member A sends heartbeat with subscription change\n  3. Member B sends leave request\n  4. Metadata update with new topic added arrives\n  5. All three events queue up for execution in the coordinator executor\n  6. Event 1 triggers epoch bump to 11 (subscription change)\n  7. Event 2 triggers epoch bump to 12 (member leave)\n  8. Event 3 triggers epoch bump to 13 (metadata refresh)\n  9. But if events 1 and 3 compute assignment independently, both might call `group.nextGroupEpoch()` multiple times\n  10. Result: Group epoch becomes 14 or 15, but members only see 11, causing future fencing errors\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testGroupEpochBumpIdempotencyDuringConcurrentOperations() throws Exception {\n      String groupId = \"test-group\";\n\n      // Setup: Create group with 3 members\n      String member1 = \"member-1\";\n      String member2 = \"member-2\";\n      String member3 = \"member-3\";\n\n      // Join all members\n      for (String memberId : Arrays.asList(member1, member2, member3)) {\n          ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData request = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n              .setGroupId(groupId)\n              .setMemberId(memberId)\n              .setMemberEpoch(0);\n          context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(request);\n      }\n      context.tick();\n\n      ConsumerGroup group = context.groupMetadataManager.getGroup(groupId);\n      int initialEpoch = group.groupEpoch();\n\n      // Now trigger multiple epoch-bumping events concurrently\n\n      // Event 1: Member 1 changes subscription\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData subscriptionChange =\n          new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n              .setGroupId(groupId)\n              .setMemberId(member1)\n              .setMemberEpoch(group.members().get(member1).memberEpoch())\n              .setSubscribedTopicNames(Arrays.asList(\"topic-new\")); These cleanup operations run asynchronously and independently of incoming offset commit requests.\n\n  The code does not prevent concurrent access to the same offset record during cleanup and commit. If an offset commit is being persisted while a cleanup task is removing the offset, the final state could be:\n  - Offset is persisted from commit\n  - Cleanup removes it\n  - But newer offset value is not visible because the record was already deleted\n  - Or the offset is partially updated leading to corruption\n\n**Scenario**:\n  1. Member commits offset {topic-A-0: 100} at time T1\n  2. Offset record is queued for persistence\n  3. Cleanup task wakes up at T2 and determines the offset has expired (based on retention config)\n  4. Cleanup deletes the offset record (generates tombstone)\n  5. Commit record arrives at storage layer after tombstone\n  6. Storage layer orders them: delete (tombstone), then commit\n  7. Final state: offset is gone, but member thinks it committed successfully\n  8. On consumer restart, offset 100 is lost, causing message reprocessing or data loss\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testOffsetExpirationDoesNotCancelInflightCommits() throws Exception {\n      String groupId = \"test-group\";\n      String memberId = \"member-1\";\n      TopicPartition tp = new TopicPartition(\"test-topic\", 0);\n\n      // Join member to group\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData joinRequest = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(0);\n      context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(joinRequest);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Verify member is in group\n      ConsumerGroup group = context.groupMetadataManager.getGroup(groupId);\n      assertTrue(group.hasMember(memberId));\n\n      // Commit offset\n      OffsetCommitRequestData commitRequest = new OffsetCommitRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setGenerationId(1)\n          .setTopics(Arrays.asList(\n              new OffsetCommitRequestData.OffsetCommitRequestTopic()\n                  .setName(tp.topic())\n                  .setPartitions(Arrays.asList(\n                      new OffsetCommitRequestData.OffsetCommitRequestPartition()\n                          .setPartitionIndex(tp.partition())\n                          .setCommittedOffset(100)\n                          .setCommittedLeaderEpoch(0)\n                  ))\n          ));\n\n      // Commit offset (not yet persisted)\n      CoordinatorResult<OffsetCommitResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> commitResult =\n          context.commitOffset(commitRequest);\n\n      // Verify commit was accepted\n      assertEquals(Errors.NONE.code(),\n          commitResult.response().topics().get(0).partitions().get(0).errorCode());\n\n      // Simulate cleanup task running: mark offset as expired\n      // This is tricky - we need to simulate the cleanup task\n      // by advancing time or mocking the offset retention check\n\n      // Trigger cleanup with TTL = very short (or advance time)\n      context.advanceTime(TimeUnit.DAYS.toMillis(365));  // 1 year of expiration\n      context.cleanupGroupMetadata();\n      context.tick();  // Process cleanup records\n\n      // Verify: The committed offset should still be visible\n      // (either the commit persisted after cleanup, or cleanup respected inflight commits)\n      OffsetFetchRequestData fetchRequest = new OffsetFetchRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setTopics(Arrays.asList(\n              new OffsetFetchRequestData.OffsetFetchRequestTopic()\n                  .setName(tp.topic())\n                  .setPartitionIndexes(Arrays.asList(tp.partition()))\n          ));\n\n      CoordinatorResult<OffsetFetchResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> fetchResult =\n          context.fetchOffsets(fetchRequest);\n\n      // The offset should either:\n      // 1. Be present with value 100 (cleanup respected inflight commit), OR\n      // 2. Be absent with clear error (cleanup completed before commit)\n      // But NOT be partially updated or corrupted\n      var offsetInfo = fetchResult.response().topics().get(0)\n          .partitions().get(0);\n\n      if (offsetInfo.errorCode() == Errors.NONE.code()) {\n          // Offset was committed before cleanup\n          assertEquals(100, offsetInfo.committedOffset());\n      } else {\n          // Offset was cleaned up - acceptable if cleanup won the race\n          assertEquals(Errors.NO_OFFSET.code(), offsetInfo.errorCode());\n      }\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Coverage Delta**: This test would exercise:\n  - Offset cleanup scheduling (GroupCoordinatorShard line 983: cleanupGroupMetadata)\n  - Group deletion logic (lines 8542: maybeDeleteGroup with offset expiration)\n  - Concurrent offset commit and cleanup operations (OffsetMetadataManager integration)\n  - Offset state consistency (lines 8542-8560: group deletion with offset cleanup)\n  - Record ordering guarantees (GroupCoordinatorShard append logic)\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 5: Share Group State Machine Violation During Concurrent Heartbeats\n\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 4932, 1595-1615 (Share group epoch validation), ShareGroup.java state transitions\n- **Description**:\n  Share groups have their own state machine separate from consumer groups. The `shareGroupHeartbeat()` method at line 4932 handles member state transitions. The member epoch validation at line 1595-1615 checks if member epochs are valid.\n\n  However, the Share group state machine may allow certain transitions that are illegal. For example:\n  - A member in state ASSIGNED can transition to REVOKED if it receives revocation instructions\n  - But if two heartbeats arrive out of order, state could be violated (e.g., REVOKED -> ASSIGNED -> REVOKED is invalid)\n  - The code lacks atomic state transition checks that would prevent this\n\n**Scenario**:\n  1. Share group member is in ASSIGNED state (has partitions)\n  2. Coordinator assigns new target: member should move to REVOKED state\n  3. Member sends heartbeat 1: acknowledges revocation, moves to REVOKED\n  4. Member sends heartbeat 2: (delayed/old) claims ASSIGNED state with old partitions\n  5. If heartbeat 2 is processed after heartbeat 1 due to reordering:\n     - First: Member transitions ASSIGNED -> REVOKED (correct)\n     - Then: Member transitions REVOKED -> ASSIGNED (invalid!)\n  6. Final state: Member is ASSIGNED but coordinator thinks REVOKED, partition owned by no one\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testShareGroupMemberStateTransitionValidation() throws Exception {\n      String groupId = \"share-group\";\n      String memberId = \"share-member-1\";\n\n      // Setup: Create share group with member\n      ShareGroupHeartbeatRequestData joinRequest = new ShareGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(0)\n          .setRebalanceTimeoutMs(6000);\n\n      CoordinatorResult<ShareGroupHeartbeatResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> result =\n          context.shareGroupHeartbeat(joinRequest);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Verify member is ASSIGNED\n      ShareGroup group = context.groupMetadataManager.getGroup(groupId);\n      ShareGroupMember member = group.members().get(memberId);\n      int currentEpoch = member.memberEpoch();\n\n      // Trigger revocation assignment\n      // (This would normally happen via assignment computation, simulating here)\n      context.triggerShareGroupRebalance(groupId);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Member should now be in REVOKED state expecting revocation ACK\n      member = group.members().get(memberId);\n      assertEquals(\"Member should be REVOKED after rebalance\",\n          ShareGroupMember.State.REVOKED, member.state());\n\n      // Now simulate out-of-order heartbeat delivery:\n      // Heartbeat 1: Member acknowledges revocation (correct)\n      ShareGroupHeartbeatRequestData revocationAck = new ShareGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(currentEpoch + 1)  // Bumped epoch for new assignment\n          .setStateId(0);  // Acknowledgment of no revocation (cleared)\n\n      // Heartbeat 2: Old heartbeat re-sent claiming old assignment (should be rejected)\n      ShareGroupHeartbeatRequestData oldHeartbeat = new ShareGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(currentEpoch)  // Old epoch\n          .setStateId(1);  // Old state with assignment\n\n      // Process revocation ACK first\n      CoordinatorResult<ShareGroupHeartbeatResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> ackResult =\n          context.shareGroupHeartbeat(revocationAck);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Process old heartbeat after (simulating reordering)\n      CoordinatorResult<ShareGroupHeartbeatResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> oldResult =\n          context.shareGroupHeartbeat(oldHeartbeat);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Verify: Old heartbeat should be rejected with FENCED_MEMBER_EPOCH\n      assertTrue(\"Old heartbeat should be fenced\",\n          oldResult.response().errorCode() == Errors.FENCED_MEMBER_EPOCH.code());\n\n      // Verify member is NOT in invalid state\n      member = group.members().get(memberId);\n      assertNotEquals(\"Member should not revert to ASSIGNED after being REVOKED\",\n          ShareGroupMember.State.ASSIGNED, member.state());\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Coverage Delta**: This test would exercise:\n  - Share group heartbeat processing (lines 4932: shareGroupHeartbeat)\n  - Member epoch validation for share groups (lines 1595-1615: throwIfShareGroupMemberEpochIsInvalid)\n  - State machine transitions in share groups (ShareGroup state management)\n  - Out-of-order message handling (concurrent heartbeat processing)\n  - Member state consistency validation\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 6: Member Revocation Timeout Expiration with Concurrent Metadata Refresh\n\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 4641, 5924-5961, 4189-4206 (member fencing)\n- **Description**:\n  Consumer group members entering the UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS state have a rebalance timeout scheduled (line 4641: `scheduleConsumerGroupRebalanceTimeout`). If this timeout expires, the member is fenced (line 4189: `consumerGroupFenceMember`).\n\n  However, if a metadata update arrives at the exact same time as the rebalance timeout expiration, both code paths may try to fence the member simultaneously. The metadata update at line 5955-5960 calls `requestMetadataRefresh()` which may trigger a new target assignment computation, while the timeout handler fences the member. These are not synchronized, leading to:\n  - Member is fenced by timeout\n  - Metadata update triggers rebalance\n  - New target assignment includes the fenced member\n  - Member state is corrupted (simultaneously in UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS and fenced)\n\n**Scenario**:\n  1. Member in UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS state, rebalance timeout scheduled for T+5s\n  2. At T+4.9s, metadata update with new topic arrives\n  3. onMetadataUpdate() at line 5924 processes delta\n  4. At T+5.0s (concurrent), rebalance timeout fires\n  5. Timeout handler calls consumerGroupFenceMember() at line 4189\n  6. Metadata handler is still executing requestMetadataRefresh() at line 5955\n  7. Both try to update the same member simultaneously:\n     - Timeout: removes member, fences with epoch LEAVE_GROUP_MEMBER_EPOCH\n     - Metadata: adds member to groups needing rebalance\n  8. Result: Member appears in both fenced and active lists, state is inconsistent\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testMemberRevocationTimeoutDoesNotRaceWithMetadataRefresh() throws Exception {\n      String groupId = \"test-group\";\n      String memberId = \"member-1\";\n\n      // Setup: Create group with member\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData joinRequest = new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId)\n          .setMemberEpoch(0);\n      context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(joinRequest);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Trigger rebalance by adding new topic subscription\n      ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData updateSubscription =\n          new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n              .setGroupId(groupId)\n              .setMemberId(memberId)\n              .setMemberEpoch(1)\n              .setSubscribedTopicNames(Arrays.asList(\"new-topic\"));\n\n      context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(updateSubscription);\n      context.tick();\n\n      // Member should now be in UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS with rebalance timeout\n      ConsumerGroup group = context.groupMetadataManager.getGroup(groupId);\n      ConsumerGroupMember member = group.members().get(memberId);\n      assertEquals(\"Member should be in revocation state\",\n          MemberState.UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS, member.state());\n\n      int memberEpoch = member.memberEpoch();\n\n      // Now simulate concurrent events:\n      // 1. Metadata update arrives\n      // 2. Rebalance timeout fires\n\n      // Record the current scheduled timeouts\n      List<ExpiredTimeout> expiredTimeouts = context.getExpiredTimeouts(\n          context.time().milliseconds() + context.config().rebalanceTimeoutMs() + 100);\n\n      // Trigger metadata update that affects the topic subscriptions\n      TopicRecord newTopic = new TopicRecord()\n          .setVersion((short)0)\n          .setName(\"new-topic\")\n          .setId(Uuid.randomUuid());\n\n      MetadataDelta delta = new MetadataDelta(context.metadataImage());\n      // Simulate partition count change requiring rebalance\n      context.onMetadataUpdate(delta, delta.image());\n\n      // Now advance time to trigger rebalance timeout\n      // (This should happen concurrently with metadata update in reality)\n      context.advanceTime(context.config().rebalanceTimeoutMs() + 1000);\n      context.tick();  // Process all timeouts and metadata updates\n      context.tick();  // Process resulting records\n\n      // Verify consistency: Member should be in exactly one state\n      ConsumerGroup finalGroup = context.groupMetadataManager.getGroup(groupId);\n      ConsumerGroupMember finalMember = finalGroup.members().get(memberId);\n\n      // Member should either:\n      // 1. Still be in group (if metadata refresh happened first), OR\n      // 2. Be removed (if timeout fenced first)\n      // But NOT in both states\n\n      if (finalMember != null) {\n          // Member is still in group\n          assertTrue(\"Member in group should be in stable state\",\n              finalMember.state() == MemberState.STABLE ||\n              finalMember.state() == MemberState.UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS);\n      }\n      // else: Member was fenced/removed, which is also valid\n\n      // Key assertion: No inconsistent state\n      Set<String> activeMembers = finalGroup.members().keySet();\n      Set<String> fencedMembers = finalGroup.fencedMembers().keySet();\n\n      assertTrue(\"Member cannot be in both active and fenced lists\",\n          !activeMembers.contains(memberId) || !fencedMembers.contains(memberId));\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Coverage Delta**: This test would exercise:\n  -
